150208 I desire therefore that the men in every place pray, lifting up holy hands without anger and doubting.
150209 In the same way, that women also adorn themselves in decent clothing, with modesty and propriety; not just with braided hair, gold, pearls, or expensive clothing;
150210 but (which becomes women professing godliness) with good works.
150211 Let a woman learn in quietness with all subjection.
150212 But I don't permit a woman to teach, nor to exercise authority over a man, but to be in quietness.
150213 For Adam was first formed, then Eve.
150214 Adam wasn't deceived, but the woman, being deceived, has fallen into disobedience;
150215 but she will be saved through her childbearing, if they continue in faith, love, and sanctification with sobriety.
150301 This is a faithful saying: if a man seeks the office of an overseer, he desires a good work.
150302 The overseer therefore must be without reproach, the husband of one wife, temperate, sensible, modest, hospitable, good at teaching;
150303 not a drinker, not violent, not greedy for money, but gentle, not quarrelsome, not covetous;
150304 one who rules his own house well, having children in subjection with all reverence;
150305 (but if a man doesn't know how to rule his own house, how will he take care of the assembly of God?)
150306 not a new convert, lest being puffed up he fall into the same condemnation as the devil.
150307 Moreover he must have good testimony from those who are outside, to avoid falling into reproach and the snare of the devil.
150308 Servants, in the same way, must be reverent, not double-tongued, not addicted to much wine, not greedy for money;
150309 holding the mystery of the faith in a pure conscience.
150310 Let them also first be tested; then let them serve if they are blameless.
150311 Their wives in the same way must be reverent, not slanderers, temperate, faithful in all things.
150312 Let servants be husbands of one wife, ruling their children and their own houses well.
150313 For those who have served well gain for themselves a good standing, and great boldness in the faith which is in Christ Jesus.
150314 These things I write to you, hoping to come to you shortly;
150315 but if I wait long, that you may know how men ought to behave themselves in the house of God, which is the assembly of the living God, the pillar and ground of the truth.
150316 Without controversy, the mystery of godliness is great: God was revealed in the flesh, justified in the spirit, seen by angels, preached among the nations, believed on in the world, and received up in glory.
150401 But the Spirit says expressly that in later times some will fall away from the faith, paying attention to seducing spirits and doctrines of demons,
150402 through the hypocrisy of men who speak lies, branded in their own conscience as with a hot iron;
150403 forbidding marriage and commanding to abstain from foods which God created to be received with thanksgiving by those who believe and know the truth.
150404 For every creature of God is good, and nothing is to be rejected, if it is received with thanksgiving.
150405 For it is sanctified through the word of God and prayer.
150406 If you instruct the brothers of these things, you will be a good servant of Christ Jesus, nourished in the words of the faith, and of the good doctrine which you have followed.
150407 But refuse profane and old wives' fables. Exercise yourself toward godliness.
150408 For bodily exercise has some value, but godliness has value in all things, having the promise of the life which is now, and of that which is to come.
150409 This saying is faithful and worthy of all acceptance.
150410 For to this end we both labor and suffer reproach, because we have set our trust in the living God, who is the Savior of all men, especially of those who believe.
150411 Command and teach these things.
150412 Let no man despise your youth; but be an example to those who believe, in word, in your way of life, in love, in spirit, in faith, and in purity.
150413 Until I come, pay attention to reading, to exhortation, and to teaching.
150414 Don't neglect the gift that is in you, which was given to you by prophecy, with the laying on of the hands of the elders.
150415 Be diligent in these things. Give yourself wholly to them, that your progress may be revealed to all.
150416 Pay attention to yourself, and to your teaching. Continue in these things, for in doing this you will save both yourself and those who hear you.
150501 Don't rebuke an older man, but exhort him as a father; the younger men as brothers;
150502 the elder women as mothers; the younger as sisters, in all purity.
150503 Honor widows who are widows indeed.
150504 But if any widow has children or grandchildren, let them learn first to show piety towards their own family, and to repay their parents, for this is acceptable in the sight of God.
150505 Now she who is a widow indeed, and desolate, has her hope set on God, and continues in petitions and prayers night and day.
150506 But she who gives herself to pleasure is dead while she lives.
150507 Also command these things, that they may be without reproach.
150508 But if anyone doesn't provide for his own, and especially his own household, he has denied the faith, and is worse than an unbeliever.
150509 Let no one be enrolled as a widow under sixty years old, having been the wife of one man,
150510 being approved by good works, if she has brought up children, if she has been hospitable to strangers, if she has washed the saints' feet, if she has relieved the afflicted, and if she has diligently followed every good work.
150511 But refuse younger widows, for when they have grown wanton against Christ, they desire to marry;
150512 having condemnation, because they have rejected their first pledge.
150513 Besides, they also learn to be idle, going about from house to house. Not only idle, but also gossips and busybodies, saying things which they ought not.
150514 I desire therefore that the younger widows marry, bear children, rule the household, and give no occasion to the adversary for reviling.
150515 For already some have turned aside after Satan.
150516 If any man or woman who believes has widows, let them relieve them, and don't let the assembly be burdened; that it might relieve those who are widows indeed.
150517 Let the elders who rule well be counted worthy of double honor, especially those who labor in the word and in teaching.
150518 For the Scripture says, "You shall not muzzle the ox when it treads out the grain." And, "The laborer is worthy of his wages."
150519 Don't receive an accusation against an elder, except at the word of two or three witnesses.
150520 Those who sin, reprove in the sight of all, that the rest also may be in fear.
150521 I command you in the sight of God, and Christ Jesus, and the chosen angels, that you observe these things without prejudice, doing nothing by partiality.
150522 Lay hands hastily on no one, neither be a participant in other men's sins. Keep yourself pure.
150523 Be no longer a drinker of water only, but use a little wine for your stomach's sake and your frequent infirmities.
150524 Some men's sins are evident, preceding them to judgment, and some also follow later.
150525 In the same way also there are good works that are obvious, and those that are otherwise can't be hidden.
150601 Let as many as are bondservants under the yoke count their own masters worthy of all honor, that the name of God and the doctrine not be blasphemed.
150602 Those who have believing masters, let them not despise them, because they are brothers, but rather let them serve them, because those who partake of the benefit are believing and beloved. Teach and exhort these things.
150603 If anyone teaches a different doctrine, and doesn't consent to sound words, the words of our Lord Jesus Christ, and to the doctrine which is according to godliness,
150604 he is conceited, knowing nothing, but obsessed with arguments, disputes, and word battles, from which come envy, strife, reviling, evil suspicions,
150605 constant friction of people of corrupt minds and destitute of the truth, who suppose that godliness is a means of gain. Withdraw yourself from such.
150606 But godliness with contentment is great gain.
150607 For we brought nothing into the world, and we certainly can't carry anything out.
150608 But having food and clothing, we will be content with that.
150609 But those who are determined to be rich fall into a temptation and a snare and many foolish and harmful lusts, such as drown men in ruin and destruction.
150610 For the love of money is a root of all kinds of evil. Some have been led astray from the faith in their greed, and have pierced themselves through with many sorrows.
150611 But you, man of God, flee these things, and follow after righteousness, godliness, faith, love, patience, and gentleness.
150612 Fight the good fight of faith. Lay hold of the eternal life to which you were called, and you confessed the good confession in the sight of many witnesses.
150613 I command you before God, who gives life to all things, and before Christ Jesus, who before Pontius Pilate testified the good confession,
150614 that you keep the commandment without spot, blameless, until the appearing of our Lord Jesus Christ;
150615 which in its own times he will show, who is the blessed and only Ruler, the King of kings, and Lord of lords;
150616 who alone has immortality, dwelling in unapproachable light; whom no man has seen, nor can see: to whom be honor and eternal power. Amen.
150617 Charge those who are rich in this present world that they not be haughty, nor have their hope set on the uncertainty of riches, but on the living God, who richly provides us with everything to enjoy;
150618 that they do good, that they be rich in good works, that they be ready to distribute, willing to communicate;
150619 laying up in store for themselves a good foundation against the time to come, that they may lay hold of eternal life.
150620 Timothy, guard that which is committed to you, turning away from the empty chatter and oppositions of the knowledge which is falsely so called;
150621 which some professing have erred concerning the faith. Grace be with you. Amen.
160101 Paul, an apostle of Jesus Christ through the will of God, according to the promise of the life which is in Christ Jesus,
160102 to Timothy, my beloved child: Grace, mercy, and peace, from God the Father and Christ Jesus our Lord.
160103 I thank God, whom I serve as my forefathers did, with a pure conscience. How unceasing is my memory of you in my petitions, night and day
160104 longing to see you, remembering your tears, that I may be filled with joy;
160105 having been reminded of the unfeigned faith that is in you; which lived first in your grandmother Lois, and your mother Eunice, and, I am persuaded, in you also.
160106 For this cause, I remind you that you should stir up the gift of God which is in you through the laying on of my hands.
160107 For God didn't give us a spirit of fear, but of power, love, and self-control.
160108 Therefore don't be ashamed of the testimony of our Lord, nor of me his prisoner; but endure hardship for the Good News according to the power of God,
160109 who saved us and called us with a holy calling, not according to our works, but according to his own purpose and grace, which was given to us in Christ Jesus before times eternal,
160110 but has now been revealed by the appearing of our Savior, Christ Jesus, who abolished death, and brought life and immortality to light through the Good News.
160111 For this, I was appointed as a preacher, an apostle, and a teacher of the Gentiles.
160112 For this cause I also suffer these things. Yet I am not ashamed, for I know him whom I have believed, and I am persuaded that he is able to guard that which I have committed to him against that day.
160113 Hold the pattern of sound words which you have heard from me, in faith and love which is in Christ Jesus.
160114 That good thing which was committed to you, guard through the Holy Spirit who dwells in us.
160115 This you know, that all who are in Asia turned away from me; of whom are Phygelus and Hermogenes.
160116 May the Lord grant mercy to the house of Onesiphorus, for he often refreshed me, and was not ashamed of my chain,
160117 but when he was in Rome, he sought me diligently, and found me
160118 (the Lord grant to him to find the Lord's mercy in that day); and in how many things he served at Ephesus, you know very well.
160201 You therefore, my child, be strengthened in the grace that is in Christ Jesus.
160202 The things which you have heard from me among many witnesses, commit the same to faithful men, who will be able to teach others also.
160203 You therefore must endure hardship, as a good soldier of Christ Jesus.
160204 No soldier on duty entangles himself in the affairs of life, that he may please him who enrolled him as a soldier.
160205 Also, if anyone competes in athletics, he isn't crowned unless he has competed by the rules.
160206 The farmers who labor must be the first to get a share of the crops.
160207 Consider what I say, and may the Lord give you understanding in all things.
160208 Remember Jesus Christ, risen from the dead, of the seed of David, according to my Good News,
160209 in which I suffer hardship to the point of chains as a criminal. But God's word isn't chained.
160210 Therefore I endure all things for the chosen ones' sake, that they also may obtain the salvation which is in Christ Jesus with eternal glory.
160211 This saying is faithful: "For if we died with him, we will also live with him.
160212 If we endure, we will also reign with him. If we deny him, he also will deny us.
160213 If we are faithless, he remains faithful. He can't deny himself."
160214 Remind them of these things, charging them in the sight of the Lord, that they don't argue about words, to no profit, to the subverting of those who hear.
160215 Give diligence to present yourself approved by God, a workman who doesn't need to be ashamed, properly handling the Word of Truth.
160216 But shun empty chatter, for they will proceed further in ungodliness,
160217 and their word will consume like gangrene, of whom is Hymenaeus and Philetus;
160218 men who have erred concerning the truth, saying that the resurrection is already past, and overthrowing the faith of some.
160219 However God's firm foundation stands, having this seal, "The Lord knows those who are his," and, "Let every one who names the name of the Lord depart from unrighteousness."
160220 Now in a large house there are not only vessels of gold and of silver, but also of wood and of clay. Some are for honor, and some for dishonor.
160221 If anyone therefore purges himself from these, he will be a vessel for honor, sanctified, and suitable for the master's use, prepared for every good work.
160222 Flee from youthful lusts; but pursue righteousness, faith, love, and peace with those who call on the Lord out of a pure heart.
160223 But refuse foolish and ignorant questionings, knowing that they generate strife.
160224 The Lord's servant must not quarrel, but be gentle towards all, able to teach, patient,
160225 in gentleness correcting those who oppose him: perhaps God may give them repentance leading to a full knowledge of the truth,
160226 and they may recover themselves out of the devil's snare, having been taken captive by him to his will.
160301 But know this, that in the last days, grievous times will come.
160302 For men will be lovers of self, lovers of money, boastful, arrogant, blasphemers, disobedient to parents, unthankful, unholy,
160303 without natural affection, unforgiving, slanderers, without self-control, fierce, no lovers of good,
160304 traitors, headstrong, conceited, lovers of pleasure rather than lovers of God;
160305 holding a form of godliness, but having denied the power thereof. Turn away from these, also.
160306 For of these are those who creep into houses, and take captive gullible women loaded down with sins, led away by various lusts,
160307 always learning, and never able to come to the knowledge of the truth.
160308 Even as Jannes and Jambres opposed Moses, so do these also oppose the truth; men corrupted in mind, reprobate concerning the faith.
160309 But they will proceed no further. For their folly will be evident to all men, as theirs also came to be.
160310 But you did follow my teaching, conduct, purpose, faith, patience, love, steadfastness,
160311 persecutions, and sufferings: those things that happened to me at Antioch, Iconium, and Lystra. I endured those persecutions. Out of them all the Lord delivered me.
160312 Yes, and all who desire to live godly in Christ Jesus will suffer persecution.
160313 But evil men and impostors will grow worse and worse, deceiving and being deceived.
160314 But you remain in the things which you have learned and have been assured of, knowing from whom you have learned them.
160315 From infancy, you have known the holy Scriptures which are able to make you wise for salvation through faith, which is in Christ Jesus.
160316 Every Scripture is God-breathed and profitable for teaching, for reproof, for correction, and for instruction in righteousness,
160317 that the man of God may be complete, thoroughly equipped for every good work.
160401 I command you therefore before God and the Lord Jesus Christ, who will judge the living and the dead at his appearing and his Kingdom:
160402 preach the word; be urgent in season and out of season; reprove, rebuke, and exhort, with all patience and teaching.
160403 For the time will come when they will not listen to the sound doctrine, but, having itching ears, will heap up for themselves teachers after their own lusts;
160404 and will turn away their ears from the truth, and turn aside to fables.
160405 But you be sober in all things, suffer hardship, do the work of an evangelist, and fulfill your ministry.
160406 For I am already being offered, and the time of my departure has come.
160407 I have fought the good fight. I have finished the course. I have kept the faith.
160408 From now on, there is stored up for me the crown of righteousness, which the Lord, the righteous judge, will give to me on that day; and not to me only, but also to all those who have loved his appearing.
160409 Be diligent to come to me soon,
160410 for Demas left me, having loved this present world, and went to Thessalonica; Crescens to Galatia, and Titus to Dalmatia.
160411 Only Luke is with me. Take Mark, and bring him with you, for he is useful to me for service.
160412 But I sent Tychicus to Ephesus.
160413 Bring the cloak that I left at Troas with Carpus when you come, and the books, especially the parchments.
160414 Alexander, the coppersmith, did much evil to me. The Lord will repay him according to his works,
160415 of whom you also must beware; for he greatly opposed our words.
160416 At my first defense, no one came to help me, but all left me. May it not be held against them.
160417 But the Lord stood by me, and strengthened me, that through me the message might be fully proclaimed, and that all the Gentiles might hear; and I was delivered out of the mouth of the lion.
160418 And the Lord will deliver me from every evil work, and will preserve me for his heavenly Kingdom; to whom be the glory forever and ever. Amen.
160419 Greet Prisca and Aquila, and the house of Onesiphorus.
160420 Erastus remained at Corinth, but I left Trophimus at Miletus sick.
160421 Be diligent to come before winter. Eubulus salutes you, as do Pudens, Linus, Claudia, and all the brothers.
160422 The Lord Jesus Christ be with your spirit. Grace be with you. Amen.
170101 Paul, a servant of God, and an apostle of Jesus Christ, according to the faith of God's chosen ones, and the knowledge of the truth which is according to godliness,
170102 in hope of eternal life, which God, who can't lie, promised before time began;
170103 but in his own time revealed his word in the message with which I was entrusted according to the commandment of God our Savior;
170104 to Titus, my true child according to a common faith: Grace, mercy, and peace from God the Father and the Lord Jesus Christ our Savior.
170105 I left you in Crete for this reason, that you would set in order the things that were lacking, and appoint elders in every city, as I directed you;
170106 if anyone is blameless, the husband of one wife, having children who believe, who are not accused of loose or unruly behavior.
170107 For the overseer must be blameless, as God's steward; not self-pleasing, not easily angered, not given to wine, not violent, not greedy for dishonest gain;
170108 but given to hospitality, as a lover of good, sober minded, fair, holy, self-controlled;
170109 holding to the faithful word which is according to the teaching, that he may be able to exhort in the sound doctrine, and to convict those who contradict him.
170110 For there are also many unruly men, vain talkers and deceivers, especially those of the circumcision,
170111 whose mouths must be stopped; men who overthrow whole houses, teaching things which they ought not, for dishonest gain's sake.
170112 One of them, a prophet of their own, said, "Cretans are always liars, evil beasts, and idle gluttons."
170113 This testimony is true. For this cause, reprove them sharply, that they may be sound in the faith,
170114 not paying attention to Jewish fables and commandments of men who turn away from the truth.
170115 To the pure, all things are pure; but to those who are defiled and unbelieving, nothing is pure; but both their mind and their conscience are defiled.
170116 They profess that they know God, but by their works they deny him, being abominable, disobedient, and unfit for any good work.
170201 But say the things which fit sound doctrine,
170202 that older men should be temperate, sensible, sober minded, sound in faith, in love, and in patience:
170203 and that older women likewise be reverent in behavior, not slanderers nor enslaved to much wine, teachers of that which is good;
170204 that they may train the young women to love their husbands, to love their children,
170205 to be sober minded, chaste, workers at home, kind, being in subjection to their own husbands, that God's word may not be blasphemed.
170206 Likewise, exhort the younger men to be sober minded;
170207 in all things showing yourself an example of good works; in your teaching showing integrity, seriousness, incorruptibility,
170208 and soundness of speech that can't be condemned; that he who opposes you may be ashamed, having no evil thing to say about us.
170209 Exhort servants to be in subjection to their own masters, and to be well-pleasing in all things; not contradicting;
170210 not stealing, but showing all good fidelity; that they may adorn the doctrine of God, our Savior, in all things.
170211 For the grace of God has appeared, bringing salvation to all men,
170212 instructing us to the intent that, denying ungodliness and worldly lusts, we would live soberly, righteously, and godly in this present world;
170213 looking for the blessed hope and appearing of the glory of our great God and Savior, Jesus Christ;
170214 who gave himself for us, that he might redeem us from all iniquity, and purify for himself a people for his own possession, zealous for good works.
170215 Say these things and exhort and reprove with all authority. Let no man despise you.
170301 Remind them to be in subjection to rulers and to authorities, to be obedient, to be ready for every good work,
170302 to speak evil of no one, not to be contentious, to be gentle, showing all humility toward all men.
170303 For we were also once foolish, disobedient, deceived, serving various lusts and pleasures, living in malice and envy, hateful, and hating one another.
170304 But when the kindness of God our Savior and his love toward mankind appeared,
170305 not by works of righteousness, which we did ourselves, but according to his mercy, he saved us, through the washing of regeneration and renewing by the Holy Spirit,
170306 whom he poured out on us richly, through Jesus Christ our Savior;
170307 that, being justified by his grace, we might be made heirs according to the hope of eternal life.
170308 This saying is faithful, and concerning these things I desire that you affirm confidently, so that those who have believed God may be careful to maintain good works. These things are good and profitable to men;
170309 but shun foolish questionings, genealogies, strife, and disputes about the law; for they are unprofitable and vain.
170310 Avoid a factious man after a first and second warning;
170311 knowing that such a one is perverted, and sins, being self-condemned.
170312 When I send Artemas to you, or Tychicus, be diligent to come to me to Nicopolis, for I have determined to winter there.
170313 Send Zenas, the lawyer, and Apollos on their journey speedily, that nothing may be lacking for them.
170314 Let our people also learn to maintain good works for necessary uses, that they may not be unfruitful.
170315 All who are with me greet you. Greet those who love us in faith. Grace be with you all. Amen.
180101 Paul, a prisoner of Christ Jesus, and Timothy our brother, to Philemon, our beloved fellow worker,
180102 to the beloved Apphia, to Archippus, our fellow soldier, and to the assembly in your house:
180103 Grace to you and peace from God our Father and the Lord Jesus Christ.
180104 I thank my God always, making mention of you in my prayers,
180105 hearing of your love, and of the faith which you have toward the Lord Jesus, and toward all the saints;
180106 that the fellowship of your faith may become effective, in the knowledge of every good thing which is in us in Christ Jesus.
180107 For we have much joy and comfort in your love, because the hearts of the saints have been refreshed through you, brother.
180108 Therefore, though I have all boldness in Christ to command you that which is appropriate,
180109 yet for love's sake I rather beg, being such a one as Paul, the aged, but also a prisoner of Jesus Christ.
180110 I beg you for my child, whom I have become the father of in my chains, Onesimus,
180111 who once was useless to you, but now is useful to you and to me.
180112 I am sending him back. Therefore receive him, that is, my own heart,
180113 whom I desired to keep with me, that on your behalf he might serve me in my chains for the Good News.
180114 But I was willing to do nothing without your consent, that your goodness would not be as of necessity, but of free will.
180115 For perhaps he was therefore separated from you for a while, that you would have him forever,
180116 no longer as a slave, but more than a slave, a beloved brother, especially to me, but how much rather to you, both in the flesh and in the Lord.
180117 If then you count me a partner, receive him as you would receive me.
180118 But if he has wronged you at all, or owes you anything, put that to my account.
180119 I, Paul, write this with my own hand: I will repay it (not to mention to you that you owe to me even your own self besides).
180120 Yes, brother, let me have joy from you in the Lord. Refresh my heart in the Lord.
180121 Having confidence in your obedience, I write to you, knowing that you will do even beyond what I say.
180122 Also, prepare a guest room for me, for I hope that through your prayers I will be restored to you.
180123 Epaphras, my fellow prisoner in Christ Jesus, greets you,
180124 as do Mark, Aristarchus, Demas, and Luke, my fellow workers.
180125 The grace of our Lord Jesus Christ be with your spirit. Amen.
190101 God, having in the past spoken to the fathers through the prophets at many times and in various ways,
190102 has at the end of these days spoken to us by his Son, whom he appointed heir of all things, through whom also he made the worlds.
190103 His Son is the radiance of his glory, the very image of his substance, and upholding all things by the word of his power, when he had by himself made purification for our sins, sat down on the right hand of the Majesty on high;
190104 having become so much better than the angels, as he has inherited a more excellent name than they have.
190105 For to which of the angels did he say at any time, "You are my Son. Today have I become your father?" and again, "I will be to him a Father, and he will be to me a Son?"
190106 Again, when he brings in the firstborn into the world he says, "Let all the angels of God worship him."
190107 Of the angels he says, "Who makes his angels winds, and his servants a flame of fire."
190108 But of the Son he says, "Your throne, O God, is forever and ever. The scepter of uprightness is the scepter of your Kingdom.
190109 You have loved righteousness, and hated iniquity; therefore God, your God, has anointed you with the oil of gladness above your fellows."
190110 And, "You, Lord, in the beginning, laid the foundation of the earth. The heavens are the works of your hands.
190111 They will perish, but you continue. They all will grow old like a garment does.
190112 As a mantle, you will roll them up, and they will be changed; but you are the same. Your years will not fail."
190113 But which of the angels has he told at any time, "Sit at my right hand, until I make your enemies the footstool of your feet?"
190114 Aren't they all serving spirits, sent out to do service for the sake of those who will inherit salvation?
190201 Therefore we ought to pay greater attention to the things that were heard, lest perhaps we drift away.
190202 For if the word spoken through angels proved steadfast, and every transgression and disobedience received a just recompense;
190203 how will we escape if we neglect so great a salvation--which at the first having been spoken through the Lord, was confirmed to us by those who heard;
190204 God also testifying with them, both by signs and wonders, by various works of power, and by gifts of the Holy Spirit, according to his own will?
190205 For he didn't subject the world to come, of which we speak, to angels.
190206 But one has somewhere testified, saying, "What is man, that you think of him? Or the son of man, that you care for him?
190207 You made him a little lower than the angels. You crowned him with glory and honor.
190208 You have put all things in subjection under his feet." For in that he subjected all things to him, he left nothing that is not subject to him. But now we don't see all things subjected to him, yet.
190209 But we see him who has been made a little lower than the angels, Jesus, because of the suffering of death crowned with glory and honor, that by the grace of God he should taste of death for everyone.
190210 For it became him, for whom are all things, and through whom are all things, in bringing many children to glory, to make the author of their salvation perfect through sufferings.
190211 For both he who sanctifies and those who are sanctified are all from one, for which cause he is not ashamed to call them brothers,
190212 saying, "I will declare your name to my brothers. In the midst of the congregation I will sing your praise."
190213 Again, "I will put my trust in him." Again, "Behold, here I am with the children whom God has given me."
190214 Since then the children have shared in flesh and blood, he also himself in like manner partook of the same, that through death he might bring to nothing him who had the power of death, that is, the devil,
190215 and might deliver all of them who through fear of death were all their lifetime subject to bondage.
190216 For most certainly, he doesn't give help to angels, but he gives help to the seed of Abraham.
190217 Therefore he was obligated in all things to be made like his brothers, that he might become a merciful and faithful high priest in things pertaining to God, to make atonement for the sins of the people.
190218 For in that he himself has suffered being tempted, he is able to help those who are tempted.
190301 Therefore, holy brothers, partakers of a heavenly calling, consider the Apostle and High Priest of our confession, Jesus;
190302 who was faithful to him who appointed him, as also was Moses in all his house.
190303 For he has been counted worthy of more glory than Moses, inasmuch as he who built the house has more honor than the house.
190304 For every house is built by someone; but he who built all things is God.
190305 Moses indeed was faithful in all his house as a servant, for a testimony of those things which were afterward to be spoken,
190306 but Christ is faithful as a Son over his house; whose house we are, if we hold fast our confidence and the glorying of our hope firm to the end.
190307 Therefore, even as the Holy Spirit says, "Today if you will hear his voice,
190308 don't harden your hearts, as in the rebellion, like as in the day of the trial in the wilderness,
190309 where your fathers tested me by proving me, and saw my works for forty years.
190310 Therefore I was displeased with that generation, and said, 'They always err in their heart, but they didn't know my ways;'
190311 as I swore in my wrath, 'They will not enter into my rest.'"
190312 Beware, brothers, lest perhaps there be in any one of you an evil heart of unbelief, in falling away from the living God;
190313 but exhort one another day by day, so long as it is called "today;" lest any one of you be hardened by the deceitfulness of sin.
190314 For we have become partakers of Christ, if we hold fast the beginning of our confidence firm to the end:
190315 while it is said, "Today if you will hear his voice, don't harden your hearts, as in the rebellion."
190316 For who, when they heard, rebelled? No, didn't all those who came out of Egypt by Moses?
190317 With whom was he displeased forty years? Wasn't it with those who sinned, whose bodies fell in the wilderness?
190318 To whom did he swear that they wouldn't enter into his rest, but to those who were disobedient?
190319 We see that they were not able to enter in because of unbelief.
190401 Let us fear therefore, lest perhaps anyone of you should seem to have come short of a promise of entering into his rest.
190402 For indeed we have had good news preached to us, even as they also did, but the word they heard didn't profit them, because it wasn't mixed with faith by those who heard.
190403 For we who have believed do enter into that rest, even as he has said, "As I swore in my wrath, they will not enter into my rest;" although the works were finished from the foundation of the world.
190404 For he has said this somewhere about the seventh day, "God rested on the seventh day from all his works;"
190405 and in this place again, "They will not enter into my rest."
190406 Seeing therefore it remains that some should enter therein, and they to whom the good news was before preached failed to enter in because of disobedience,
190407 he again defines a certain day, today, saying through David so long a time afterward (just as has been said), "Today if you will hear his voice, don't harden your hearts."
190408 For if Joshua had given them rest, he would not have spoken afterward of another day.
190409 There remains therefore a Sabbath rest for the people of God.
190410 For he who has entered into his rest has himself also rested from his works, as God did from his.
190411 Let us therefore give diligence to enter into that rest, lest anyone fall after the same example of disobedience.
190412 For the word of God is living, and active, and sharper than any two-edged sword, and piercing even to the dividing of soul and spirit, of both joints and marrow, and is able to discern the thoughts and intentions of the heart.
190413 There is no creature that is hidden from his sight, but all things are naked and laid open before the eyes of him with whom we have to do.
190414 Having then a great high priest, who has passed through the heavens, Jesus, the Son of God, let us hold tightly to our confession.
190415 For we don't have a high priest who can't be touched with the feeling of our infirmities, but one who has been in all points tempted like we are, yet without sin.
190416 Let us therefore draw near with boldness to the throne of grace, that we may receive mercy, and may find grace for help in time of need.
190501 For every high priest, being taken from among men, is appointed for men in things pertaining to God, that he may offer both gifts and sacrifices for sins.
190502 The high priest can deal gently with those who are ignorant and going astray, because he himself is also surrounded with weakness.
190503 Because of this, he must offer sacrifices for sins for the people, as well as for himself.
190504 Nobody takes this honor on himself, but he is called by God, just like Aaron was.
190505 So also Christ didn't glorify himself to be made a high priest, but it was he who said to him, "You are my Son. Today I have become your father."
190506 As he says also in another place, "You are a priest forever, after the order of Melchizedek."
190507 He, in the days of his flesh, having offered up prayers and petitions with strong crying and tears to him who was able to save him from death, and having been heard for his godly fear,
190508 though he was a Son, yet learned obedience by the things which he suffered.
190509 Having been made perfect, he became to all of those who obey him the author of eternal salvation,
190510 named by God a high priest after the order of Melchizedek.
190511 About him we have many words to say, and hard to interpret, seeing you have become dull of hearing.
190512 For when by reason of the time you ought to be teachers, you again need to have someone teach you the rudiments of the first principles of the oracles of God. You have come to need milk, and not solid food.
190513 For everyone who lives on milk is not experienced in the word of righteousness, for he is a baby.
190514 But solid food is for those who are full grown, who by reason of use have their senses exercised to discern good and evil.
190601 Therefore leaving the teaching of the first principles of Christ, let us press on to perfection--not laying again a foundation of repentance from dead works, of faith toward God,
190602 of the teaching of baptisms, of laying on of hands, of resurrection of the dead, and of eternal judgment.
190603 This will we do, if God permits.
190604 For concerning those who were once enlightened and tasted of the heavenly gift, and were made partakers of the Holy Spirit,
190605 and tasted the good word of God, and the powers of the age to come,
190606 and then fell away, it is impossible to renew them again to repentance; seeing they crucify the Son of God for themselves again, and put him to open shame.
190607 For the land which has drunk the rain that comes often on it, and brings forth a crop suitable for them for whose sake it is also tilled, receives blessing from God;
190608 but if it bears thorns and thistles, it is rejected and near being cursed, whose end is to be burned.
190609 But, beloved, we are persuaded of better things for you, and things that accompany salvation, even though we speak like this.
190610 For God is not unrighteous, so as to forget your work and the labor of love which you showed toward his name, in that you served the saints, and still do serve them.
190611 We desire that each one of you may show the same diligence to the fullness of hope even to the end,
190612 that you won't be sluggish, but imitators of those who through faith and patience inherited the promises.
190613 For when God made a promise to Abraham, since he could swear by none greater, he swore by himself,
190614 saying, "Surely blessing I will bless you, and multiplying I will multiply you."
190615 Thus, having patiently endured, he obtained the promise.
190616 For men indeed swear by a greater one, and in every dispute of theirs the oath is final for confirmation.
190617 In this way God, being determined to show more abundantly to the heirs of the promise the immutability of his counsel, interposed with an oath;
190618 that by two immutable things, in which it is impossible for God to lie, we may have a strong encouragement, who have fled for refuge to take hold of the hope set before us.
190619 This hope we have as an anchor of the soul, a hope both sure and steadfast and entering into that which is within the veil;
190620 where as a forerunner Jesus entered for us, having become a high priest forever after the order of Melchizedek.
190701 For this Melchizedek, king of Salem, priest of God Most High, who met Abraham returning from the slaughter of the kings and blessed him,
190702 to whom also Abraham divided a tenth part of all (being first, by interpretation, king of righteousness, and then also king of Salem, which is king of peace;
190703 without father, without mother, without genealogy, having neither beginning of days nor end of life, but made like the Son of God), remains a priest continually.
190704 Now consider how great this man was, to whom even Abraham, the patriarch, gave a tenth out of the best spoils.
190705 They indeed of the sons of Levi who receive the priest's office have a commandment to take tithes of the people according to the law, that is, of their brothers, though these have come out of the body of Abraham,
190706 but he whose genealogy is not counted from them has accepted tithes from Abraham, and has blessed him who has the promises.
190707 But without any dispute the lesser is blessed by the greater.
190708 Here people who die receive tithes, but there one receives tithes of whom it is testified that he lives.
190709 We can say that through Abraham even Levi, who receives tithes, has paid tithes,
190710 for he was yet in the body of his father when Melchizedek met him.
190711 Now if there was perfection through the Levitical priesthood (for under it the people have received the law), what further need was there for another priest to arise after the order of Melchizedek, and not be called after the order of Aaron?
190712 For the priesthood being changed, there is of necessity a change made also in the law.
190713 For he of whom these things are said belongs to another tribe, from which no one has officiated at the altar.
190714 For it is evident that our Lord has sprung out of Judah, about which tribe Moses spoke nothing concerning priesthood.
190715 This is yet more abundantly evident, if after the likeness of Melchizedek there arises another priest,
190716 who has been made, not after the law of a fleshly commandment, but after the power of an endless life:
190717 for it is testified, "You are a priest forever, according to the order of Melchizedek."
190718 For there is an annulling of a foregoing commandment because of its weakness and uselessness
190719 (for the law made nothing perfect), and a bringing in of a better hope, through which we draw near to God.
190720 Inasmuch as he was not made priest without the taking of an oath
190721 (for they indeed have been made priests without an oath), but he with an oath by him that says of him, "The Lord swore and will not change his mind, 'You are a priest forever, according to the order of Melchizedek.'"
190722 By so much, Jesus has become the collateral of a better covenant.
190723 Many, indeed, have been made priests, because they are hindered from continuing by death.
190724 But he, because he lives forever, has his priesthood unchangeable.
190725 Therefore he is also able to save to the uttermost those who draw near to God through him, seeing that he lives forever to make intercession for them.
190726 For such a high priest was fitting for us: holy, guiltless, undefiled, separated from sinners, and made higher than the heavens;
190727 who doesn't need, like those high priests, to offer up sacrifices daily, first for his own sins, and then for the sins of the people. For he did this once for all, when he offered up himself.
190728 For the law appoints men as high priests who have weakness, but the word of the oath which came after the law appoints a Son forever who has been perfected.
190801 Now in the things which we are saying, the main point is this. We have such a high priest, who sat down on the right hand of the throne of the Majesty in the heavens,
190802 a servant of the sanctuary, and of the true tabernacle, which the Lord pitched, not man.
190803 For every high priest is appointed to offer both gifts and sacrifices. Therefore it is necessary that this high priest also have something to offer.
190804 For if he were on earth, he would not be a priest at all, seeing there are priests who offer the gifts according to the law;
190805 who serve a copy and shadow of the heavenly things, even as Moses was warned by God when he was about to make the tabernacle, for he said, "See, you shall make everything according to the pattern that was shown to you on the mountain."
190806 But now he has obtained a more excellent ministry, by so much as he is also the mediator of a better covenant, which on better promises has been given as law.
190807 For if that first covenant had been faultless, then no place would have been sought for a second.
190808 For finding fault with them, he said, "Behold, the days come," says the Lord, "that I will make a new covenant with the house of Israel and with the house of Judah;
190809 not according to the covenant that I made with their fathers, in the day that I took them by the hand to lead them out of the land of Egypt; for they didn't continue in my covenant, and I disregarded them," says the Lord.
190810 "For this is the covenant that I will make with the house of Israel. After those days," says the Lord; "I will put my laws into their mind, I will also write them on their heart. I will be their God, and they will be my people.
190811 They will not teach every man his fellow citizen, and every man his brother, saying, 'Know the Lord,' for all will know me, from the least of them to the greatest of them.
190812 For I will be merciful to their unrighteousness. I will remember their sins and lawless deeds no more."
190813 In that he says, "A new covenant," he has made the first old. But that which is becoming old and grows aged is near to vanishing away.
190901 Now indeed even the first covenant had ordinances of divine service, and an earthly sanctuary.
190902 For a tabernacle was prepared. In the first part were the lampstand, the table, and the show bread; which is called the Holy Place.
190903 After the second veil was the tabernacle which is called the Holy of Holies,
190904 having a golden altar of incense, and the ark of the covenant overlaid on all sides with gold, in which was a golden pot holding the manna, Aaron's rod that budded, and the tablets of the covenant;
190905 and above it cherubim of glory overshadowing the mercy seat, of which things we can't speak now in detail.
190906 Now these things having been thus prepared, the priests go in continually into the first tabernacle, accomplishing the services,
190907 but into the second the high priest alone, once in the year, not without blood, which he offers for himself, and for the errors of the people.
190908 The Holy Spirit is indicating this, that the way into the Holy Place wasn't yet revealed while the first tabernacle was still standing;
190909 which is a symbol of the present age, where gifts and sacrifices are offered that are incapable, concerning the conscience, of making the worshipper perfect;
190910 being only (with meats and drinks and various washings) fleshly ordinances, imposed until a time of reformation.
190911 But Christ having come as a high priest of the coming good things, through the greater and more perfect tabernacle, not made with hands, that is to say, not of this creation,
190912 nor yet through the blood of goats and calves, but through his own blood, entered in once for all into the Holy Place, having obtained eternal redemption.
190913 For if the blood of goats and bulls, and the ashes of a heifer sprinkling those who have been defiled, sanctify to the cleanness of the flesh:
190914 how much more will the blood of Christ, who through the eternal Spirit offered himself without blemish to God, cleanse your conscience from dead works to serve the living God?
190915 For this reason he is the mediator of a new covenant, since a death has occurred for the redemption of the transgressions that were under the first covenant, that those who have been called may receive the promise of the eternal inheritance.
190916 For where a last will and testament is, there must of necessity be the death of him who made it.
190917 For a will is in force where there has been death, for it is never in force while he who made it lives.
190918 Therefore even the first covenant has not been dedicated without blood.
190919 For when every commandment had been spoken by Moses to all the people according to the law, he took the blood of the calves and the goats, with water and scarlet wool and hyssop, and sprinkled both the book itself and all the people,
190920 saying, "This is the blood of the covenant which God has commanded you."
190921 Moreover he sprinkled the tabernacle and all the vessels of the ministry in like manner with the blood.
190922 According to the law, nearly everything is cleansed with blood, and apart from shedding of blood there is no remission.
190923 It was necessary therefore that the copies of the things in the heavens should be cleansed with these; but the heavenly things themselves with better sacrifices than these.
190924 For Christ hasn't entered into holy places made with hands, which are representations of the true, but into heaven itself, now to appear in the presence of God for us;
190925 nor yet that he should offer himself often, as the high priest enters into the holy place year by year with blood not his own,
190926 or else he must have suffered often since the foundation of the world. But now once at the end of the ages, he has been revealed to put away sin by the sacrifice of himself.
190927 Inasmuch as it is appointed for men to die once, and after this, judgment,
190928 so Christ also, having been offered once to bear the sins of many, will appear a second time, without sin, to those who are eagerly waiting for him for salvation.
191001 For the law, having a shadow of the good to come, not the very image of the things, can never with the same sacrifices year by year, which they offer continually, make perfect those who draw near.
191002 Or else wouldn't they have ceased to be offered, because the worshippers, having been once cleansed, would have had no more consciousness of sins?
191003 But in those sacrifices there is yearly reminder of sins.
191004 For it is impossible that the blood of bulls and goats should take away sins.
191005 Therefore when he comes into the world, he says, "Sacrifice and offering you didn't desire, but you prepared a body for me;
191006 You had no pleasure in whole burnt offerings and sacrifices for sin.
191007 Then I said, 'Behold, I have come (in the scroll of the book it is written of me) to do your will, O God.'"
191008 Previously saying, "Sacrifices and offerings and whole burnt offerings and sacrifices for sin you didn't desire, neither had pleasure in them" (those which are offered according to the law),
191009 then he has said, "Behold, I have come to do your will." He takes away the first, that he may establish the second,
191010 by which will we have been sanctified through the offering of the body of Jesus Christ once for all.
191011 Every priest indeed stands day by day serving and often offering the same sacrifices, which can never take away sins,
191012 but he, when he had offered one sacrifice for sins forever, sat down on the right hand of God;
191013 from that time waiting until his enemies are made the footstool of his feet.
191014 For by one offering he has perfected forever those who are being sanctified.
191015 The Holy Spirit also testifies to us, for after saying,
191016 "This is the covenant that I will make with them: 'After those days,' says the Lord, 'I will put my laws on their heart, I will also write them on their mind;'" then he says,
191017 "I will remember their sins and their iniquities no more."
191018 Now where remission of these is, there is no more offering for sin.
191019 Having therefore, brothers, boldness to enter into the holy place by the blood of Jesus,
191020 by the way which he dedicated for us, a new and living way, through the veil, that is to say, his flesh;
191021 and having a great priest over the house of God,
191022 let's draw near with a true heart in fullness of faith, having our hearts sprinkled from an evil conscience, and having our body washed with pure water,
191023 let us hold fast the confession of our hope without wavering; for he who promised is faithful.
191024 Let us consider how to provoke one another to love and good works,
191025 not forsaking our own assembling together, as the custom of some is, but exhorting one another; and so much the more, as you see the Day approaching.
191026 For if we sin willfully after we have received the knowledge of the truth, there remains no more a sacrifice for sins,
191027 but a certain fearful expectation of judgment, and a fierceness of fire which will devour the adversaries.
191028 A man who disregards Moses' law dies without compassion on the word of two or three witnesses.
191029 How much worse punishment, do you think, will he be judged worthy of, who has trodden under foot the Son of God, and has counted the blood of the covenant with which he was sanctified an unholy thing, and has insulted the Spirit of grace?
191030 For we know him who said, "Vengeance belongs to me," says the Lord, "I will repay." Again, "The Lord will judge his people."
191031 It is a fearful thing to fall into the hands of the living God.
191032 But remember the former days, in which, after you were enlightened, you endured a great struggle with sufferings;
191033 partly, being exposed to both reproaches and oppressions; and partly, becoming partakers with those who were treated so.
191034 For you both had compassion on me in my chains, and joyfully accepted the plundering of your possessions, knowing that you have for yourselves a better possession and an enduring one in the heavens.
191035 Therefore don't throw away your boldness, which has a great reward.
191036 For you need endurance so that, having done the will of God, you may receive the promise.
191037 "In a very little while, he who comes will come, and will not wait.
191038 But the righteous will live by faith. If he shrinks back, my soul has no pleasure in him."
191039 But we are not of those who shrink back to destruction, but of those who have faith to the saving of the soul.
191101 Now faith is assurance of things hoped for, proof of things not seen.
191102 For by this, the elders obtained testimony.
191103 By faith, we understand that the universe has been framed by the word of God, so that what is seen has not been made out of things which are visible.
191104 By faith, Abel offered to God a more excellent sacrifice than Cain, through which he had testimony given to him that he was righteous, God testifying with respect to his gifts; and through it he, being dead, still speaks.
191105 By faith, Enoch was taken away, so that he wouldn't see death, and he was not found, because God translated him. For he has had testimony given to him that before his translation he had been well pleasing to God.
191106 Without faith it is impossible to be well pleasing to him, for he who comes to God must believe that he exists, and that he is a rewarder of those who seek him.
191107 By faith, Noah, being warned about things not yet seen, moved with godly fear, prepared a ship for the saving of his house, through which he condemned the world, and became heir of the righteousness which is according to faith.
191108 By faith, Abraham, when he was called, obeyed to go out to the place which he was to receive for an inheritance. He went out, not knowing where he went.
191109 By faith, he lived as an alien in the land of promise, as in a land not his own, dwelling in tents, with Isaac and Jacob, the heirs with him of the same promise.
191110 For he looked for the city which has the foundations, whose builder and maker is God.
191111 By faith, even Sarah herself received power to conceive, and she bore a child when she was past age, since she counted him faithful who had promised.
191112 Therefore as many as the stars of the sky in multitude, and as innumerable as the sand which is by the sea shore, were fathered by one man, and him as good as dead.
191113 These all died in faith, not having received the promises, but having seen them and embraced them from afar, and having confessed that they were strangers and pilgrims on the earth.
191114 For those who say such things make it clear that they are seeking a country of their own.
191115 If indeed they had been thinking of that country from which they went out, they would have had enough time to return.
191116 But now they desire a better country, that is, a heavenly one. Therefore God is not ashamed of them, to be called their God, for he has prepared a city for them.
191117 By faith, Abraham, being tested, offered up Isaac. Yes, he who had gladly received the promises was offering up his one and only son;
191118 even he to whom it was said, "In Isaac will your seed be called;"
191119 concluding that God is able to raise up even from the dead. Figuratively speaking, he also did receive him back from the dead.
191120 By faith, Isaac blessed Jacob and Esau, even concerning things to come.
191121 By faith, Jacob, when he was dying, blessed each of the sons of Joseph, and worshiped, leaning on the top of his staff.
191122 By faith, Joseph, when his end was near, made mention of the departure of the children of Israel; and gave instructions concerning his bones.
191123 By faith, Moses, when he was born, was hidden for three months by his parents, because they saw that he was a beautiful child, and they were not afraid of the king's commandment.
191124 By faith, Moses, when he had grown up, refused to be called the son of Pharaoh's daughter,
191125 choosing rather to share ill treatment with God's people, than to enjoy the pleasures of sin for a time;
191126 accounting the reproach of Christ greater riches than the treasures of Egypt; for he looked to the reward.
191127 By faith, he left Egypt, not fearing the wrath of the king; for he endured, as seeing him who is invisible.
191128 By faith, he kept the Passover, and the sprinkling of the blood, that the destroyer of the firstborn should not touch them.
191129 By faith, they passed through the Red Sea as on dry land. When the Egyptians tried to do so, they were swallowed up.
191130 By faith, the walls of Jericho fell down, after they had been encircled for seven days.
191131 By faith, Rahab the prostitute, didn't perish with those who were disobedient, having received the spies in peace.
191132 What more shall I say? For the time would fail me if I told of Gideon, Barak, Samson, Jephthah, David, Samuel, and the prophets;
191133 who, through faith subdued kingdoms, worked out righteousness, obtained promises, stopped the mouths of lions,
191134 quenched the power of fire, escaped the edge of the sword, from weakness were made strong, grew mighty in war, and caused foreign armies to flee.
191135 Women received their dead by resurrection. Others were tortured, not accepting their deliverance, that they might obtain a better resurrection.
191136 Others were tried by mocking and scourging, yes, moreover by bonds and imprisonment.
191137 They were stoned. They were sawn apart. They were tempted. They were slain with the sword. They went around in sheep skins and in goat skins; being destitute, afflicted, ill-treated
191138 (of whom the world was not worthy), wandering in deserts, mountains, caves, and the holes of the earth.
191139 These all, having had testimony given to them through their faith, didn't receive the promise,
191140 God having provided some better thing concerning us, so that apart from us they should not be made perfect.
191201 Therefore let us also, seeing we are surrounded by so great a cloud of witnesses, lay aside every weight and the sin which so easily entangles us, and let us run with patience the race that is set before us,
191202 looking to Jesus, the author and perfecter of faith, who for the joy that was set before him endured the cross, despising its shame, and has sat down at the right hand of the throne of God.
191203 For consider him who has endured such contradiction of sinners against himself, that you don't grow weary, fainting in your souls.
191204 You have not yet resisted to blood, striving against sin;
191205 and you have forgotten the exhortation which reasons with you as with children, "My son, don't take lightly the chastening of the Lord, nor faint when you are reproved by him;
191206 For whom the Lord loves, he chastens, and scourges every son whom he receives."
191207 It is for discipline that you endure. God deals with you as with children, for what son is there whom his father doesn't discipline?
191208 But if you are without discipline, of which all have been made partakers, then are you illegitimate, and not children.
191209 Furthermore, we had the fathers of our flesh to chasten us, and we paid them respect. Shall we not much rather be in subjection to the Father of spirits, and live?
191210 For they indeed, for a few days, punished us as seemed good to them; but he for our profit, that we may be partakers of his holiness.
191211 All chastening seems for the present to be not joyous but grievous; yet afterward it yields the peaceful fruit of righteousness to those who have been exercised thereby.
191212 Therefore, lift up the hands that hang down and the feeble knees,
191213 and make straight paths for your feet, so that which is lame may not be dislocated, but rather be healed.
191214 Follow after peace with all men, and the sanctification without which no man will see the Lord,
191215 looking carefully lest there be any man who falls short of the grace of God; lest any root of bitterness springing up trouble you, and many be defiled by it;
191216 lest there be any sexually immoral person, or profane person, like Esau, who sold his birthright for one meal.
191217 For you know that even when he afterward desired to inherit the blessing, he was rejected, for he found no place for a change of mind though he sought it diligently with tears.
191218 For you have not come to a mountain that might be touched, and that burned with fire, and to blackness, darkness, storm,
191219 the sound of a trumpet, and the voice of words; which those who heard it begged that not one more word should be spoken to them,
191220 for they could not stand that which was commanded, "If even an animal touches the mountain, it shall be stoned;"
191221 and so fearful was the appearance, that Moses said, "I am terrified and trembling."
191222 But you have come to Mount Zion, and to the city of the living God, the heavenly Jerusalem, and to innumerable multitudes of angels,
191223 to the general assembly and assembly of the firstborn who are enrolled in heaven, to God the Judge of all, to the spirits of just men made perfect,
191224 to Jesus, the mediator of a new covenant, and to the blood of sprinkling that speaks better than that of Abel.
191225 See that you don't refuse him who speaks. For if they didn't escape when they refused him who warned on the Earth, how much more will we not escape who turn away from him who warns from heaven,
191226 whose voice shook the earth then, but now he has promised, saying, "Yet once more I will shake not only the earth, but also the heavens."
191227 This phrase, "Yet once more," signifies the removing of those things that are shaken, as of things that have been made, that those things which are not shaken may remain.
191228 Therefore, receiving a Kingdom that can't be shaken, let us have grace, through which we serve God acceptably, with reverence and awe,
191229 for our God is a consuming fire.
191301 Let brotherly love continue.
191302 Don't forget to show hospitality to strangers, for in doing so, some have entertained angels without knowing it.
191303 Remember those who are in bonds, as bound with them; and those who are ill-treated, since you are also in the body.
191304 Let marriage be held in honor among all, and let the bed be undefiled: but God will judge the sexually immoral and adulterers.
191305 Be free from the love of money, content with such things as you have, for he has said, "I will in no way leave you, neither will I in any way forsake you."
191306 So that with good courage we say, "The Lord is my helper. I will not fear. What can man do to me?"
191307 Remember your leaders, men who spoke to you the word of God, and considering the results of their conduct, imitate their faith.
191308 Jesus Christ is the same yesterday, today, and forever.
191309 Don't be carried away by various and strange teachings, for it is good that the heart be established by grace, not by food, through which those who were so occupied were not benefited.
191310 We have an altar from which those who serve the holy tabernacle have no right to eat.
191311 For the bodies of those animals, whose blood is brought into the holy place by the high priest as an offering for sin, are burned outside of the camp.
191312 Therefore Jesus also, that he might sanctify the people through his own blood, suffered outside of the gate.
191313 Let us therefore go out to him outside of the camp, bearing his reproach.
191314 For we don't have here an enduring city, but we seek that which is to come.
191315 Through him, then, let us offer up a sacrifice of praise to God continually, that is, the fruit of lips which proclaim allegiance to his name.
191316 But don't forget to be doing good and sharing, for with such sacrifices God is well pleased.
191317 Obey your leaders and submit to them, for they watch on behalf of your souls, as those who will give account, that they may do this with joy, and not with groaning, for that would be unprofitable for you.
191318 Pray for us, for we are persuaded that we have a good conscience, desiring to live honorably in all things.
191319 I strongly urge you to do this, that I may be restored to you sooner.
191320 Now may the God of peace, who brought again from the dead the great shepherd of the sheep with the blood of an eternal covenant, our Lord Jesus,
191321 make you complete in every good work to do his will, working in you that which is well pleasing in his sight, through Jesus Christ, to whom be the glory forever and ever. Amen.
191322 But I exhort you, brothers, endure the word of exhortation, for I have written to you in few words.
191323 Know that our brother Timothy has been freed, with whom, if he comes shortly, I will see you.
191324 Greet all of your leaders and all the saints. The Italians greet you.
191325 Grace be with you all. Amen.
200101 James, a servant of God and of the Lord Jesus Christ, to the twelve tribes which are in the Dispersion: Greetings.
200102 Count it all joy, my brothers, when you fall into various temptations,
200103 knowing that the testing of your faith produces endurance.
200104 Let endurance have its perfect work, that you may be perfect and complete, lacking in nothing.
200105 But if any of you lacks wisdom, let him ask of God, who gives to all liberally and without reproach; and it will be given to him.
200106 But let him ask in faith, without any doubting, for he who doubts is like a wave of the sea, driven by the wind and tossed.
200107 For let that man not think that he will receive anything from the Lord.
200108 He is a double-minded man, unstable in all his ways.
200109 But let the brother in humble circumstances glory in his high position;
200110 and the rich, in that he is made humble, because like the flower in the grass, he will pass away.
200111 For the sun arises with the scorching wind, and withers the grass, and the flower in it falls, and the beauty of its appearance perishes. So also will the rich man fade away in his pursuits.
200112 Blessed is the man who endures temptation, for when he has been approved, he will receive the crown of life, which the Lord promised to those who love him.
200113 Let no man say when he is tempted, "I am tempted by God," for God can't be tempted by evil, and he himself tempts no one.
200114 But each one is tempted, when he is drawn away by his own lust, and enticed.
200115 Then the lust, when it has conceived, bears sin; and the sin, when it is full grown, brings forth death.
200116 Don't be deceived, my beloved brothers.
200117 Every good gift and every perfect gift is from above, coming down from the Father of lights, with whom can be no variation, nor turning shadow.
200118 Of his own will he brought us forth by the word of truth, that we should be a kind of first fruits of his creatures.
200119 So, then, my beloved brothers, let every man be swift to hear, slow to speak, and slow to anger;
200120 for the anger of man doesn't produce the righteousness of God.
200121 Therefore, putting away all filthiness and overflowing of wickedness, receive with humility the implanted word, which is able to save your souls.
200122 But be doers of the word, and not only hearers, deluding your own selves.
200123 For if anyone is a hearer of the word and not a doer, he is like a man looking at his natural face in a mirror;
200124 for he sees himself, and goes away, and immediately forgets what kind of man he was.
200125 But he who looks into the perfect law of freedom, and continues, not being a hearer who forgets, but a doer of the work, this man will be blessed in what he does.
200126 If anyone among you thinks himself to be religious while he doesn't bridle his tongue, but deceives his heart, this man's religion is worthless.
200127 Pure religion and undefiled before our God and Father is this: to visit the fatherless and widows in their affliction, and to keep oneself unstained by the world.
200201 My brothers, don't hold the faith of our Lord Jesus Christ of glory with partiality.
200202 For if a man with a gold ring, in fine clothing, comes into your synagogue, and a poor man in filthy clothing also comes in;
200203 and you pay special attention to him who wears the fine clothing, and say, "Sit here in a good place;" and you tell the poor man, "Stand there," or "Sit by my footstool;"
200204 haven't you shown partiality among yourselves, and become judges with evil thoughts?
200205 Listen, my beloved brothers. Didn't God choose those who are poor in this world to be rich in faith, and heirs of the Kingdom which he promised to those who love him?
200206 But you have dishonored the poor man. Don't the rich oppress you, and personally drag you before the courts?
200207 Don't they blaspheme the honorable name by which you are called?
200208 However, if you fulfill the royal law, according to the Scripture, "You shall love your neighbor as yourself," you do well.
200209 But if you show partiality, you commit sin, being convicted by the law as transgressors.
200210 For whoever keeps the whole law, and yet stumbles in one point, he has become guilty of all.
200211 For he who said, "Do not commit adultery," also said, "Do not commit murder." Now if you do not commit adultery, but murder, you have become a transgressor of the law.
200212 So speak, and so do, as men who are to be judged by a law of freedom.
200213 For judgment is without mercy to him who has shown no mercy. Mercy triumphs over judgment.
200214 What good is it, my brothers, if a man says he has faith, but has no works? Can faith save him?
200215 And if a brother or sister is naked and in lack of daily food,
200216 and one of you tells them, "Go in peace, be warmed and filled;" and yet you didn't give them the things the body needs, what good is it?
200217 Even so faith, if it has no works, is dead in itself.
200218 Yes, a man will say, "You have faith, and I have works." Show me your faith without works, and I by my works will show you my faith.
200219 You believe that God is one. You do well. The demons also believe, and shudder.
200220 But do you want to know, vain man, that faith apart from works is dead?
200221 Wasn't Abraham our father justified by works, in that he offered up Isaac his son on the altar?
200222 You see that faith worked with his works, and by works faith was perfected;
200223 and the Scripture was fulfilled which says, "Abraham believed God, and it was accounted to him as righteousness;" and he was called the friend of God.
200224 You see then that by works, a man is justified, and not only by faith.
200225 In like manner wasn't Rahab the prostitute also justified by works, in that she received the messengers, and sent them out another way?
200226 For as the body apart from the spirit is dead, even so faith apart from works is dead.
200301 Let not many of you be teachers, my brothers, knowing that we will receive heavier judgment.
200302 For in many things we all stumble. If anyone doesn't stumble in word, the same is a perfect man, able to bridle the whole body also.
200303 Indeed, we put bits into the horses' mouths so that they may obey us, and we guide their whole body.
200304 Behold, the ships also, though they are so big and are driven by fierce winds, are yet guided by a very small rudder, wherever the pilot desires.
200305 So the tongue is also a little member, and boasts great things. See how a small fire can spread to a large forest!
200306 And the tongue is a fire. The world of iniquity among our members is the tongue, which defiles the whole body, and sets on fire the course of nature, and is set on fire by Gehenna.
200307 For every kind of animal, bird, creeping thing, and thing in the sea, is tamed, and has been tamed by mankind.
200308 But nobody can tame the tongue. It is a restless evil, full of deadly poison.
200309 With it we bless our God and Father, and with it we curse men, who are made in the image of God.
200310 Out of the same mouth comes forth blessing and cursing. My brothers, these things ought not to be so.
200311 Does a spring send out from the same opening fresh and bitter water?
200312 Can a fig tree, my brothers, yield olives, or a vine figs? Thus no spring yields both salt water and fresh water.
200313 Who is wise and understanding among you? Let him show by his good conduct that his deeds are done in gentleness of wisdom.
200314 But if you have bitter jealousy and selfish ambition in your heart, don't boast and don't lie against the truth.
200315 This wisdom is not that which comes down from above, but is earthly, sensual, and demonic.
200316 For where jealousy and selfish ambition are, there is confusion and every evil deed.
200317 But the wisdom that is from above is first pure, then peaceful, gentle, reasonable, full of mercy and good fruits, without partiality, and without hypocrisy.
200318 Now the fruit of righteousness is sown in peace by those who make peace.
200401 Where do wars and fightings among you come from? Don't they come from your pleasures that war in your members?
200402 You lust, and don't have. You kill, covet, and can't obtain. You fight and make war. You don't have, because you don't ask.
200403 You ask, and don't receive, because you ask with wrong motives, so that you may spend it for your pleasures.
200404 You adulterers and adulteresses, don't you know that friendship with the world is enmity with God? Whoever therefore wants to be a friend of the world makes himself an enemy of God.
200405 Or do you think that the Scripture says in vain, "The Spirit who lives in us yearns jealously"?
200406 But he gives more grace. Therefore it says, "God resists the proud, but gives grace to the humble."
200407 Be subject therefore to God. But resist the devil, and he will flee from you.
200408 Draw near to God, and he will draw near to you. Cleanse your hands, you sinners; and purify your hearts, you double-minded.
200409 Lament, mourn, and weep. Let your laughter be turned to mourning, and your joy to gloom.
200410 Humble yourselves in the sight of the Lord, and he will exalt you.
200411 Don't speak against one another, brothers. He who speaks against a brother and judges his brother, speaks against the law and judges the law. But if you judge the law, you are not a doer of the law, but a judge.
200412 Only one is the lawgiver, who is able to save and to destroy. But who are you to judge another?
200413 Come now, you who say, "Today or tomorrow let's go into this city, and spend a year there, trade, and make a profit."
200414 Whereas you don't know what your life will be like tomorrow. For what is your life? For you are a vapor, that appears for a little time, and then vanishes away.
200415 For you ought to say, "If the Lord wills, we will both live, and do this or that."
200416 But now you glory in your boasting. All such boasting is evil.
200417 To him therefore who knows to do good, and doesn't do it, to him it is sin.
200501 Come now, you rich, weep and howl for your miseries that are coming on you.
200502 Your riches are corrupted and your garments are moth-eaten.
200503 Your gold and your silver are corroded, and their corrosion will be for a testimony against you, and will eat your flesh like fire. You have laid up your treasure in the last days.
200504 Behold, the wages of the laborers who mowed your fields, which you have kept back by fraud, cry out, and the cries of those who reaped have entered into the ears of the Lord of Armies.
200505 You have lived delicately on the earth, and taken your pleasure. You have nourished your hearts as in a day of slaughter.
200506 You have condemned, you have murdered the righteous one. He doesn't resist you.
200507 Be patient therefore, brothers, until the coming of the Lord. Behold, the farmer waits for the precious fruit of the earth, being patient over it, until it receives the early and late rain.
200508 You also be patient. Establish your hearts, for the coming of the Lord is at hand.
200509 Don't grumble, brothers, against one another, so that you won't be judged. Behold, the judge stands at the door.
200510 Take, brothers, for an example of suffering and of patience, the prophets who spoke in the name of the Lord.
200511 Behold, we call them blessed who endured. You have heard of the patience of Job, and have seen the Lord in the outcome, and how the Lord is full of compassion and mercy.
200512 But above all things, my brothers, don't swear, neither by heaven, nor by the earth, nor by any other oath; but let your "yes" be "yes," and your "no," "no;" so that you don't fall into hypocrisy.
200513 Is any among you suffering? Let him pray. Is any cheerful? Let him sing praises.
200514 Is any among you sick? Let him call for the elders of the assembly, and let them pray over him, anointing him with oil in the name of the Lord,
200515 and the prayer of faith will heal him who is sick, and the Lord will raise him up. If he has committed sins, he will be forgiven.
200516 Confess your offenses to one another, and pray for one another, that you may be healed. The insistent prayer of a righteous person is powerfully effective.
200517 Elijah was a man with a nature like ours, and he prayed earnestly that it might not rain, and it didn't rain on the earth for three years and six months.
200518 He prayed again, and the sky gave rain, and the earth brought forth its fruit.
200519 Brothers, if any among you wanders from the truth, and someone turns him back,
200520 let him know that he who turns a sinner from the error of his way will save a soul from death, and will cover a multitude of sins.
